тАШ рдЗрдорд╛рдВ рдзрд┐рдпрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдореН ред рдЗрджрдореБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рдЪ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдХрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН - рдЗрдорд╛рдВ рдзрд┐рдпрдВ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢рд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдпреЛ рдмрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддреНрдпрдВ рддреБ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЖрднрд┐рдкреНрд▓рд╡рд┐рдХреЗрд╖реВрдХреНрдереНрдпреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрддреЛрдорд╡реГрджреНрдзреМ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдВрд╕рд┐рди рдЗрджрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдкрд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ – рдЗрдорд╛рдВ рдзрд┐рдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрдВрд╕реА рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреЛрд░реНрдиреБ рдХрдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рен. реп) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Jamison Brereton

67 (893)
Br╠еhaspati
Ay─Бsya ─Ас╣Еgirasa
12 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This is perhaps the clearest treatment of Br╠еhaspatiтАЩs role in the Vala myth and of his identity with Indra, the usual hero in the Vala story. As discussed above (see especially the introduction to IV.50), Hanns-Peter Schmidt (1968) has clearly shown that br╠е╠Бhaspa╠Бti was originally an epithet of Indra in his role as priest and formulator, a role that is highlighted in the Vala mythтАФsince Indra opens the Vala cave and frees the cows not with his normal power and violence but with song and correctly crafted verbal formulae. In this hymn Br╠еhaspati is credited with the deed, but in equivalence with Indra. The names are essentially superimposed upon each other, an equation made more obvious by their positioning: the name Br╠еhaspati opens the second half-verse of verses 3, 4, 5, 8, 9, 10, and the more transparent version of his name, Brahmaс╣Зaspati, is in the same position in verse 7. In the midst of this sequence, in the middle verse 6, we find Indra in initial position in the verse and credited with the same deed. The poet could hardly have made their identity clearer. (The final verse of the hymn [12] begins with the word Indra, here as hero of other stories, especially the Vr╠еtra myth.)
The hymn begins (vs. 1) with the primal finding and production of a true insight; the unidentified тАЬfourth oneтАЭ in the second half of the verse probably refers to the fourth, inaudible portion of speech, or the fourth formulation, which figures prominently in Vedic speculations on the nature and power of speech (see Jamison 1991: 251тАУ57). The second verse introduces the Aс╣Еgirases, the crucial partners of Br╠еhaspati/Indra in the opening of the Vala cave; they too find the truthful word. The next five verses (3тАУ8) narrate the dramatic opening of the cave and the freeing of the cows. One notes a certain irony in the poetтАЩs treatment of Vala: though the cave is first depicted as a fetter (vs. 4) and a stronghold (vs. 5), it is described with the ambiguous term тАЬguardтАЭ in verse 6 (a term as ambiguous in Sanskrit as it is in English), and then with a more sarcastic tone тАЬcow-nurturerтАЭ in verse 7 and тАЬcow herdтАЭ in verse 8.
The hymn ends with four verses celebrating the god and asking for blessings. Most interesting in this section is the final p─Бda of verse 10 (if we have rightly interpreted it), which alludes to the different poetic skills and styles of the mortal celebrants.

тАЬThis great seven-headed ceremony, born of truth our father (Aс╣Еgirasa) discovered; Ay─Бsya, thefrined of all races, engendered the fourth (genitive ration), reciting a hymn to Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: с╣Ъс╣гi Aс╣Еgirasa had ason named Bс╣Ыhaspati, who became the purohita of Indra, for the instrumental uction of the gods. His cows were stolen bythe Paс╣Зis, and taken to Vala’s city, and hidden in three plural ces. Indra urged Bс╣Ыhaspati to go with the Maruts andlook for them. Jamison Brereton

This seven-headed insightful thought here, born of truth and lofty, did our father find.
The fourth one indeed did the irrepressible one, belonging to all men, generate as he was pronouncing a solemn speech for Indra.

Griffith

THIS holy hymn, sublime and sevenheaded, sprung from eternal Law, our sire discovered.
Ayasya, friend of all men, hath engendered the fourth hymn as he sang his laud to Indra.

Diese siebenk├╢pfige Dichtung erfand unser Vater, die aus der Wahrheit geborene, hohe. Wohl ein Viertel davon brachte der allen bekannte Ayasya hervor, als er das Loblied auf Indra vortrug.

Dies siebenk├╢pfige Gebet, das aus heiliger Gesinnung entsprungene, erhabene, hat unser Vater erfunden; zum vierten Male erzeugte es der allen Menschen wohlwollende Aj─Бsia, den Spruch dem Indra singend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬReciting sincere praise, reflecting correctly, the Aс╣Еgirasas, the pious sons of the brilliant and powerful(Agni), upholding the intelligent base, the supporter of the sacrifice, praise from the beginning.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Supporter: padamrefers to Bс╣Ыhaspati, as supporting (dh─Бma), the sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Pronouncing the truth, thinking straight, the sons of heaven, the heroes of the lord,
the Aс╣Еgirases, establishing their inspired word [/laying their inspired track], pondered the first foundation of the sacrifice.

Griffith

Thinking aright, praising eternal Order, the sons of Dyaus the Asura, those heroes,
Angirases, holding the rank of sages, first honoured sacrifice’s holy statute.

Geldner

Wahrheit sprechend, redlich denkend haben die S├╢hne des Himmels, die Mannen des Asura, die Angiras┬┤ den Redekundigen zu ihrer Wegspur machend die erste Form des Opfers ersonnen.

Grassmann

Die heilige Ordnung preisend, dem Rechte nachsinnend, gedachten die S├╢hne des Himmels, des h├╢chsten Gottes Helden, die Angiras, zum S├дnger ihren Schritt lenkend (?) an die erste St├дtte des Opfers.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWith his friends (the Maruts) clamouring like geese, throwing open the (asuras’) cattle-folds made ofstone, Bс╣Ыhaspati calling aloud (desires to carry off) the cows; knowing all things he praises (the gods) andchants (their laudation).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Chants: udg─Бyat, acts the part of the Udg─Бt─Б

Jamison Brereton

Along with his comrades, who were constantly gabbling like geese, while he was throwing open the fastenings made of stone,
while he kept roaring to the cows, Br╠еhaspati both started the praise song and struck up the melody, as knowing one.

Griffith

Girt by his friends who cried with swanlike voices, bursting the stony barriers of the prison,
Brhaspati spake in thunder to the cattle, and uttered praise and song when he had found them.

Geldner

Mit den Freunden, die wie die G├дnse schrieen, die steinernen B├дnder sprengend hat Brihaspati, den K├╝hen zubr├╝llend, den Ton angestimmt und laut gesungen als Kundiger.

Grassmann

Begleitet wie von G├дnsen, von den lautsingenden Genossen, zersprengend die steinernen Klammern, die K├╝he anbr├╝llend, stimmte Brihaspati Loblied an, und erhob Gesang mit Weisheit.

Jamison Brereton

With two (gates) below, with one above, the cows standing hidden in the fetter of untruthтАФ
Br╠еhaspati, seeking light in the darkness, brought up the ruddy ones, for he opened up the three (gates).

Griffith

Apart from one, away from two above him, he drave the kine that stood in bonds of falsehood.
Brhaspati, seeking light amid the darkness, drave forth the bright cows: three he made apparent.

Geldner

Unten durch zwei, oben durch eine T├╝r hat Brihaspati die in den Banden des Unrechts versteckten K├╝he, im Dunkeln das Licht suchend, herausgeholt, denn er hatte die drei T├╝ren ge├╢ffnet.

Grassmann

Die K├╝he [Lichtstrahlen], welche unterhalb zweier [Verschl├╝sse] und oberhalb des dritten verborgen standen an den Wehren, die der Ungerechte aufgeth├╝rmt hatte, sie, die schimmernden, brachte Brihaspati, Licht in der Finsterniss suchend, heraus; denn er schloss die drei Verschl├╝sse auf. [Die zwei Verschl├╝sse sind wol West und Ost, unter denen die Abend- und Morgenstrahlen verborgen liegen, und die dritte die Himmelskuppe, oberhalb deren die Tagesstrahlen verschlossen gedacht sind].

рд╕рдГ рдмреГрд╣рд╕реНрдкрддрд┐рдГ рд╢рдпрдерд╛ рдЙрдкрд╢рдпреЗрди рд╕реНрдерд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкрд╛рдЪреАрдВ рдкрд░рд╛рдЩреНрдореБрдЦреАрдореН рдИрдореН рдЗрдорд╛рдореН рдЕрд╕реБрд░рдкреБрд░реАрдВ рд╡рд┐рднрд┐рджреНрдп рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рд░реНрдп рдЙрджрдзреЗрдГ рд╡рд▓рд╛рддреН рдореЗрдШрд░реВрдкрд╛рджрд╕реБрд░рд╛рддреН рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рд╣ рдпреБрдЧрдкрддреН рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рдЧрд╛рдореН рдПрддрд╛рдирд┐ рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдирд┐рдГ рдЕрдХреГрдиреНрддрддреН рдирд┐рд░реНрдЧрддрдордХрд╛рд░реНрд╖реАрддреНред рддрдорд╕рд╛рд╡реГрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╖реВрд╖рдГрдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рддрддрдГ рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рджреНрднрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рдЬрдирдпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд╢реВрдиреНрдирд┐рд░рдЧрдордпрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕реЛрд╜рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдХрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдЪрдиреАрдпрдВ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдж рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ ред рдХрдердорд┐рд╡ ред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕реНрддрдирдпрдиреН рд╢рдмреНрджрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рджреНрдпреМрдГ рдЗрд╡ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬResting near it, demolishing the western city, Bс╣Ыhaspati wrested at once from Vala the three, thedawn, the sun, the cow; thundering like the heaven, he proclaimed the adorable (Sun).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vala: liс╣н, the ocean, i.e.Vala in the form of a cloud; dawn, sun, cow: Bс╣Ыhaspati begetting the son, which comes into being after the timeof dawn, brought the cattle out from the folds enveloped in darkness

Jamison Brereton

Having split apart the stronghold (from front) to back, (having split apart) the lairs, at one blow he cut out the three [=dawn, sun, cow]
from the reservoir.
Br╠еhaspati found the dawn, the sun, the cow, (found) the chant while he was thundering like heaven.

Griffith

When he had cleft the lairs and western castle, he cut off three from him who held the waters.
Brhaspati discovered, while he thundered like Dyaus, the dawn, the Sun, the cow, the lightning.

Geldner

Nachdem er die Burg zerspalten hatte, da├Я sie sich hinten├╝ber legte, erl├╢ste er auf einmal die Drei aus dem Meere: Brihaspati fand die Morgenr├╢te, die Sonne, die Kuh; er fand den Gesang wie der Himmel donnernd.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra with his voice as with an (armed) hand clove Vala the defender of hte kine; desirous of themixture (of milk and Soma) he with (the Maruts)k, who were shining with person iration, destroyed Paс╣Зi andliberated the cows.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Shining with person iration: dripping ornaments, or having streaming ornaments,kс╣гarad─Бbharaс╣Зaiс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Indra cut apart Vala, the guard over the milkers, with a roar like a tool. Seeking the milk-mixture with (his comrades) anointed with sweat, he made the niggard wail: he stole the cows.

Griffith

As with a hand, so with his roaring Indra cleft Vala through, the guardian of the cattle.
Seeking the milk-draught with sweatshining comrades he stole the Pani’s kine and left him weeping.

Geldner

Indra hat den Vala, den Bewacher der Milchk├╝he, durch sein Gebr├╝ll wie mit der Hand zerschnitten. Mit den Schwei├Яbetupften die Milch suchend brachte er den Pani zum Weinen; er raubte seine K├╝he.

Grassmann

Indra zerbrach mit Krachen die H├╢hle, welche die Milchk├╝he verschloss, wie mit der Faust, und mit den schweisstriefenden Genossen die Zumischung der Milch begehrend, versetzte er den Paс╣Зi in Trauer und raubte ihm die K├╝he.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTogether with his true brilliant wealth-winning friendly (Maruts) he destroyed the detainer of the cows;Brahmaс╣Зaspati, with the showerers (of benefits), the conveyers of desirable (water), the frequenters of sacrifice,acquired wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Brahmaс╣Зaspati: lord of praise, i.e., of the three Vedas, the с╣Ъk, Yajus. and S─Бman;frequenters of sacrifice: or, those who go in lustre; or, dripping water

Jamison Brereton

With his trusty comrades blazing, with the winners of spoils, he cleaved apart the cow-nurturer.
The Lord of the Sacred Formulation reached through to the treasure with his bulls, his boars, with their hot sweat [/sweating over the
gharma pot].

Griffith

He with bright faithful Friends, winners of booty, hath rent the milker of the cows asunder.
Brhaspati with wild boars strong and mighty, sweating with heat, hath gained a rich possession.

Geldner

Mit seinen wahrhaften Freunden, den Ergl├╝henden, den Sch├дtzegewinnern hat er den Vala gesprengt, der von den Rindern sich n├дhrte. Brahmanaspati gelangte mit den Bullen, den Ebern, den vor Hitze Schwitzenden, in den Besitz des Reichtums.

Grassmann

Auch dieser Brahmanaspati zerspaltete mit den tapfern, leuchtenden, Beute gewinnenden Genossen den Verschliesser der K├╝he; mit den kr├дftigen von der Glut schwitzenden Ebern erlangte er den Schatz.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey with truthful mind searching for the cows resolved by their exploits to make him the lord of cattle;Bс╣Ыhaspati with his self-yoked (allied) mutually defending each other from reproach, set free the kind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Mutuallydefending: mitho avadyapebhiс╕е = those to whom the kine, to be protecte4d from the asura in the guise of sin,mutually resort

Jamison Brereton

With trusty mind begging the cowherd for the cows, they compelled him with their insightful thoughts.
Br╠еhaspati loosed the ruddy ones upward, with his own yokemates who protect each other from fault.

Griffith

They, longing for the kine, with faithful spirit incited with their hymns the Lord of cattle.
Brhaspati freed the radiant cows with comrades self-yoked, averting shame from one another.

Geldner

Sie eiferten wahrhaften Herzens mit Gebeten den Rinderherren an, ihn um die Rinder anflehend. Brihaspati lie├Я die K├╝he heraus mit seinen Verb├╝ndeten, die sich gegenseitig vor Unehre sch├╝tzen.

Grassmann

Diese hier setzten mit aufrichtigem Herzen den Herrn der K├╝he [Brihaspati] um K├╝he angehend, ihn durch Gebete in Bewegung; Brihaspati liess mit den sich selbst in Th├дtigkeit setzenden, Tadel gegenseitig abwehrenden [Genossen] die K├╝he heraus.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMagnifying the victorious Bс╣Ыhaspati, the showerer (of benefits), roaring in mid-heaven like a lion, letus praise him in the conflicts where heroes win, with auspicious praises.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

With our propitious thoughts strengthening him, ever roaring in his seat like a lion,
we would celebrate Br╠еhaspati the bull, victorious at the contest of
champions, victorious in every raid,

Griffith

In our assembly with auspicious praises exalting him who roareth like a lion,
Maywe, in every fight where heroes conquer, rejoice in strong Brhaspati the Victor.

Geldner

Mit lieblichen Gedichten ihn erhebend, der wie der L├╢we an seinem Stande br├╝llt, wollten wir dem Brihaspati, dem Bullen, dem im Zweikampf, in jedem Streite Siegreichen, zujubeln;

Grassmann

Den Brihaspati durch heilsame Lieder st├дrkend, ihn, der wie ein L├╢we auf seinem Lager br├╝llt, wollen wir ihm, dem Stiere, zujauchzen im Heldenkampfe, ihm, der in jeder Schlacht siegreich ist.

Elizarenkova

Men praised Brhaspati the Mighty, bringing the light within their mouths from sundry places.

Make our hope come true, our hope for the conferring of vigor. For you help even the weakling in your own ways.
Let all slighters be off, be behind (us). You two world-halves, who
set all in motion, hear this.

Fulfil the prayer that begs for vital vigour: aid in your wonted manner even the humble.
Let all our foes be turned and driven backward. Hear this, O Heaven and Earth, ye All-producers.

English translation:

тАЬIndra by his might has cleft the brow of the vast watery cloud, he has slain Ahi; he has made the sevenrivers flow; do you, heaven and earth, along with the gods, protect us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Indra; ie., Bс╣Ыhaspati

Jamison Brereton

Indra with his greatness split apart the head of the great flood, of Arbuda.
He smashed the serpent. He let flow the seven streams. O Heaven and Earth, along with the gods, further us.

Griffith

Indra with mighty strength cleft asunder the head of Arbuda the watery monster,
Slain Ahi, and set free the Seven Rivers. O Heaven and Earth, with all the Gods protect us.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдорд╣рддреА рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╕рд╛рдЧрд░, рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреЗ рдореВрд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛рд░реВрдк рд╡реЗрдж рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИред рдЙрд╕рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдХреЛ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдПред рд╡реЗрдж рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реЗ рд╕рд╛рдд рдЫрдиреНрджреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╛рд╣рд┐рдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рд░рд╛рдЬрд╕рднрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЧрдг рдХреЛ рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдкреНрд░рдж рд╕рд┐рджреНрдз рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерезреирее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡рд╛ (рдорд╣реНрдирд╛) рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдорд╣рддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди (рдорд╣рддрдГ-рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╡рд╕реНрдп-рдЕрд░реНрдмреБрджрд╕реНрдп) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдгрд╡рд╕реНрдп тАЬрдЕрд░реНрдгрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореНтАЭ [рдпрдЬреБреж резреиредрекреп рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] рд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрд╕реНрдп тАЬрд╡рд╛рдЧреНрд╡рд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдмреБрджрдореНтАЭ [рддреИреж рейредреоредрезремредрей] (рдореВрд░реНрдзрд╛рдирдВ рд╡рд┐-рдЕрднрд┐рдирддреН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░рд┐ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡реЗрджрдореН тАЬрдореВрд░реНрдзрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрдкрд░рд┐ рд╡рд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирдГтАЭ [рдпрдЬреБреж рейредрезреи рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрдГ] рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрддрдпрд╛-рдЙрджреНрдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ (рдЕрд╣рд┐рдореН-рдЕрд╣рдиреН) рдореЗрдШрдорд┐рд╡ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рд╡рд░рдХрдореН рдЕрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рдореН тАЬрдЕрд╣рд┐ рдореЗрдШрдирд╛рдотАЭ [рдирд┐рдШреж резредрезреж] рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рдирд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ (рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреВрдиреН-рдЕрд░рд┐рдгрд╛рддреН) рд╕рдкреНрддрд╕реНрдпрдиреНрджрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рдЫрдиреНрджреЛрд░реВрдкрд╛рдиреН рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╛рд╣рдд тАЬрд╕рд┐рдиреНрдзреБрд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрдГтАЭ [рд╢реж реоредрелредреиредрек] тАЬрд░рд┐рдгрд╛рддрд┐ рдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛тАЭ [рдирд┐рдШреж реиредрезрек] (рджреЗрд╡реИрдГ-рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдирдГ-рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ рд╕рднрд╛рдкреНрд░рдЬреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрдореН реерезреирее
